      <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">\n          <img alt="Hero of the Soviet Union" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="143" height="39" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d7/Order_of_Lenin_ribbon_bar.png 2x" width="40"/>\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Yuri Alekseyevich Gagarin\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="ru">\n        \xd0\xae\xcc\x81\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb9 \xd0\x90\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb5\xd0\xba\xd1\x81\xd0\xb5\xcc\x81\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb8\xd1\x87 \xd0\x93\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb3\xd0\xb0\xcc\x81\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yuri-alt-names_1-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-yuri-alt-names-1">\n          [note 1]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <small>\n        IPA:\n       </small>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">\n         [\xcb\x88j\xca\x89r\xca\xb2\xc9\xaaj \xc9\x90l\xca\xb2\xc9\xaa\xcb\x88ks\xca\xb2ej\xc9\xaav\xca\xb2\xc9\xaat\xc9\x95 \xc9\xa1\xc9\x90\xcb\x88\xc9\xa1ar\xca\xb2\xc9\xaan]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ; 9 March 1934 \xe2\x80\x93 27 March 1968) was a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">\n        Soviet\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Air_Forces" title="Soviet Air Forces">\n        pilot\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">\n        cosmonaut\n       </a>\n       . He was the first human to journey into\n       <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n        outer space\n       </a>\n       , when his\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_(spacecraft)" title="Vostok (spacecraft)">\n        Vostok\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       completed an\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       on 12 April 1961.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin became an international celebrity, and was awarded many medals and titles, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">\n        Hero of the Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       , the nation\'s highest honour.\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </a>\n       marked his only spaceflight, but he served as backup crew to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_1" title="Soyuz 1">\n        Soyuz 1\n       </a>\n       mission (which ended in a fatal crash). Gagarin later became deputy training director of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin_Cosmonaut_Training_Center" title="Yuri Gagarin Cosmonaut Training Center">\n        Cosmonaut Training Centre\n       </a>\n       outside\n       <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">\n        Moscow\n       </a>\n       , which was later named after him. Gagarin died in 1968 when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-15" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-15">\n        MiG-15\n       </a>\n       training jet he was piloting crashed. The\n       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_A%C3%A9ronautique_Internationale" title="F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration A\xc3\xa9ronautique Internationale">\n        F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration A\xc3\xa9ronautique Internationale\n       </a>\n       awards the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuri_A._Gagarin_Gold_Medal" title="Yuri A. Gagarin Gold Medal">\n        Yuri A. Gagarin Gold Medal\n       </a>\n       in his honor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7">\n         <a href="#Death">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Death\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Cause_of_jet_crash">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Cause of jet crash\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Personal_life">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Personal life\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Legacy_and_tributes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Legacy and tributes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#Legacy">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Legacy\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Tributes">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Tributes\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13">\n             <a href="#50th_anniversary">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               7.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               50th anniversary\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Honours_and_awards">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Honours and awards\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Sources">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sources\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">\n        Early life and education\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Yuri Gagarin was born in the village of\n       <a href="/wiki/Klushino" title="Klushino">\n        Klushino\n       </a>\n       , near\n       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin,_Smolensk_Oblast" title="Gagarin, Smolensk Oblast">\n        Gzhatsk\n       </a>\n       (renamed Gagarin in 1968 after his death), on 9 March 1934.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanbury2010_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hanbury2010-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       His parents worked on a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collective_farm" title="Collective farm">\n        collective farm\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time2006_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-time2006-3">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       His father, Alexei Ivanovich Gagarin was a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpenter" title="Carpenter">\n        carpenter\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bricklayer" title="Bricklayer">\n        bricklayer\n       </a>\n       , and his mother, Anna Timofeyevna Gagarina, was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Milkmaid" title="Milkmaid">\n        milkmaid\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents-alt-names_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-parents-alt-names-4">\n         [note 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenberg-About_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rosenberg-About-5">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Yuri was the third of four children: older brother Valentin, older sister Zoya, and younger brother Boris.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Like millions of people in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">\n        Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       , the Gagarin family suffered during Nazi occupation in\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       . Klushino was occupied in November 1941 during the German advance on Moscow, and an officer took over the Gagarin residence. The family was allowed to build a mud hut, approximately 3 by 3 metres (10 by 10\xc2\xa0ft) inside, on the land behind their house, where they spent a year and nine months until the end of the occupation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moskvitch2011_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moskvitch2011-7">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       His two older siblings were deported by the Germans to Poland for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OST-Arbeiter" title="OST-Arbeiter">\n        slave labour\n       </a>\n       in 1943, returning only after the war in 1945.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1946, the family moved to Gzhatsk, where Gagarin continued his secondary education.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moskvitch2011_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moskvitch2011-7">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1950, Gagarin entered into an apprenticeship at age 16 as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Foundry" title="Foundry">\n        foundryman\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lyubertsy" title="Lyubertsy">\n        Lyubertsy\n       </a>\n       Steel Plant near Moscow,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and also enrolled at a local "young workers" school for seventh grade evening classes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rian20110330_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rian20110330-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After graduating in 1951 from both the seventh grade and the vocational school (with honours in\n       <a href="/wiki/Moldmaker" title="Moldmaker">\n        moldmaking\n       </a>\n       and foundry-work),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rian20110330_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rian20110330-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       he was selected for further training at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saratov" title="Saratov">\n        Saratov\n       </a>\n       Industrial Technical School, where he studied\n       <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">\n        tractors\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20110404_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20110404-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While in Saratov, Gagarin volunteered for weekend training as a Soviet air cadet at a local flying club, where he learned to fly \xe2\x80\x94 at first in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Biplane" title="Biplane">\n        biplane\n       </a>\n       and later in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-18" title="Yakovlev Yak-18">\n        Yak-18\n       </a>\n       trainer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20110404_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20110404-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He also earned extra money as a part-time dock laborer on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">\n        Volga River\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moskvitch2011_7-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moskvitch2011-7">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Air_Force">\n        Soviet Air Force\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0,_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0,_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F,_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1420" data-file-width="1010" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg/220px-%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg/330px-%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg/440px-%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0%2C_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%2C_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92._%D0%98.%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0,_%D0%A1._%D0%A0._%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0,_%D0%AE._%D0%90._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F,_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_1966_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Valentina Gagarina,\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%AD%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0,_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%85%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0" title="ru:\xd0\xad\xd0\xb9\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb7\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb0, \xd0\xa1\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb0 \xd0\xa0\xd0\xb0\xd1\x85\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0">\n          Sima Eivazova\n         </a>\n         and Yuri Gagarin in Bulgaria in 1966\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After graduating from the technical school in 1955, the Soviet Army drafted Gagarin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rian20110330_9-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rian20110330-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On a recommendation, Gagarin was sent to the First Chkalov Air Force Pilot\'s School in\n       <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">\n        Orenburg\n       </a>\n       , and soloed in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-15" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-15">\n        MiG-15\n       </a>\n       in 1957.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rian20110330_9-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rian20110330-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Post-graduation, he was assigned to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Luostari" title="Luostari">\n        Luostari\n       </a>\n       airbase in\n       <a href="/wiki/Murmansk_Oblast" title="Murmansk Oblast">\n        Murmansk Oblast\n       </a>\n       , close to the Norwegian border, where terrible weather made flying risky. He became a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant" title="Lieutenant">\n        Lieutenant\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Air_Forces" title="Soviet Air Forces">\n        Soviet Air Forces\n       </a>\n       on 5 November 1957; on 6 November 1959 he received the rank of Senior Lieutenant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astro_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astro-11">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_space_program">\n        Soviet space program\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Selection_and_training">\n        Selection and training\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">\n        Vostok programme\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1960, after much searching and a selection process, Yuri Gagarin was chosen with 19 other pilots for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">\n        Soviet space program\n       </a>\n       . Gagarin was further selected for an elite training group known as the Sochi Six, from which the first cosmonauts of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">\n        Vostok programme\n       </a>\n       would be chosen. Gagarin and other prospective candidates were subjected to experiments designed to test physical and psychological endurance; he also underwent training for the upcoming flight. Out of the twenty selected, the eventual choices for the first launch were Gagarin and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gherman_Titov" title="Gherman Titov">\n        Gherman Titov\n       </a>\n       due to their performance during training sessions as well as their physical characteristics\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 space was limited in the small\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_(spacecraft)" title="Vostok (spacecraft)">\n        Vostok\n       </a>\n       cockpit, and both men were rather short. Gagarin was 1.57 metres (5\xc2\xa0ft 2\xc2\xa0in) tall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time2006_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-time2006-3">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In August 1960, when Gagarin was one of 20 possible candidates, a Soviet Air Force doctor evaluated his personality as follows:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        Modest; embarrasses when his humor gets a little too racy; high degree of intellectual development evident in Yuriy; fantastic memory; distinguishes himself from his colleagues by his sharp and far-ranging sense of attention to his surroundings; a well-developed imagination; quick reactions; persevering, prepares himself painstakingly for his activities and training exercises, handles celestial mechanics and mathematical formulae with ease as well as excels in higher mathematics; does not feel constrained when he has to defend his point of view if he considers himself right; appears that he understands life better than a lot of his friends.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siddiqi262q_12-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Siddiqi262q-12">\n          [10]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin was also a favoured candidate by his peers. When the 20 candidates were asked to anonymously vote for which other candidate they would like to see as the first to fly, all but three chose Gagarin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siddiqi262_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Siddiqi262-13">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of these candidates,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Khrunov" title="Yevgeny Khrunov">\n        Yevgeny Khrunov\n       </a>\n       , believed that Gagarin was very focused, and was demanding of himself and others when necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siddiqi261_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Siddiqi261-14">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin kept physically fit throughout his life, and was a keen sportsman. Cosmonaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Valery_Bykovsky" title="Valery Bykovsky">\n        Valery Bykovsky\n       </a>\n       wrote:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        Service in the Air Force made us strong, both physically and morally. All of us cosmonauts took up sports and PT seriously when we served in the Air Force. I know that Yuri Gagarin was fond of\n        <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">\n         ice hockey\n        </a>\n        . He liked to play goal keeper... I don\'t think I am wrong when I say that sports became a fixture in the life of the cosmonauts.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gavrilin2627q_15-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Gavrilin2627q-15">\n          [13]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       In addition to being a keen ice hockey player, Gagarin was also a\n       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">\n        basketball\n       </a>\n       fan, and coached the Saratov Industrial Technical School team, as well as being a referee.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louis1980_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Louis1980-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vostok_1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 12 April 1961, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_(spacecraft)#Vostok_3KA" title="Vostok (spacecraft)">\n        Vostok 3KA-3\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </a>\n       ) spacecraft with Gagarin aboard was launched from\n       <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">\n        Baikonur Cosmodrome\n       </a>\n       . Gagarin thus became both the first human to travel into\n       <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n        space\n       </a>\n       , and the first to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbit_(celestial_mechanics)" title="Orbit (celestial mechanics)">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       the Earth. His call sign was\n       <i>\n        Kedr\n       </i>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="ru">\n        \xd0\x9a\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb4\xd1\x80\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinus_sibirica" title="Pinus sibirica">\n        Siberian pine\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">\n        Cedar\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siddiqi275_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Siddiqi275-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div class="center">\n          <div class="floatnone">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">\n         <div class="haudio">\n          <div style="padding:4px 0">\n           <a href="/wiki/File:Gagarin-Poyekhali.ogg" title="File:Gagarin-Poyekhali.ogg">\n            <i>\n             Poyekhali!\n            </i>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div>\n           <div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px">\n            <audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="2.0059637188209" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Gagarin-Poyekhali.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">\n             <source data-bandwidth="125570" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (126 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/Gagarin-Poyekhali.ogg" type=\'audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"\'/>\n            </audio>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">\n           Gagarin\'s voice\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em">\n         <hr/>\n         <span>\n          <i>\n           Problems playing this file? See\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">\n            media help\n           </a>\n           .\n          </i>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The radio communication between the launch control room and Gagarin included the following dialogue at the moment of rocket launch:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        Korolev: "Preliminary stage..... intermediate..... main..... lift off! We wish you a good flight. Everything is all right."\n       </p>\n       <p>\n        Gagarin: "\n        <span lang="ru-Latn">\n         \xd0\x9f\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb5\xd1\x85\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8!\n        </span>\n        " (\n        <i>\n         Poyekhali!\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <i>\n         Let\'s go!\n        </i>\n        ).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n         <a href="#cite_note-18">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin\'s informal\n       <i>\n        poyekhali!\n       </i>\n       became a historical phrase in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">\n        Eastern Bloc\n       </a>\n       , used to refer to the beginning of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">\n        Space Age\n       </a>\n       in human history.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dushenko_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dushenko-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In his post-flight report, Gagarin recalled his experience of spaceflight, having been the first human in space:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        The feeling of weightlessness was somewhat unfamiliar compared with Earth conditions. Here, you feel as if you were hanging in a horizontal position in straps. You feel as if you are suspended.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siddiqi278q_21-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Siddiqi278q-21">\n          [19]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gagarin_Capsule.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Gagarin_Capsule.jpg/220px-Gagarin_Capsule.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Gagarin_Capsule.jpg/330px-Gagarin_Capsule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Gagarin_Capsule.jpg/440px-Gagarin_Capsule.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gagarin_Capsule.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Vostok I capsule on display at the\n         <a href="/wiki/RKK_Energiya_museum" title="RKK Energiya museum">\n          RKK Energiya museum\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Following the flight, Gagarin told the\n       <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">\n        Soviet leader\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">\n        Nikita Khrushchev\n       </a>\n       that during reentry he had whistled the tune "The Motherland Hears, The Motherland Knows" (\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="ru">\n        "\xd0\xa0\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0 \xd1\x81\xd0\xbb\xd1\x8b\xd1\x88\xd0\xb8\xd1\x82, \xd0\xa0\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0 \xd0\xb7\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb5\xd1\x82"\n       </span>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autobiography_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autobiography-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sovmusic-download_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sovmusic-download-23">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first two lines of the song are: "\n       <i>\n        The Motherland hears, the Motherland knows/Where her son flies in the sky\n       </i>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sovmusic-text_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sovmusic-text-24">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This patriotic song was written by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">\n        Dmitri Shostakovich\n       </a>\n       in 1951 (opus 86), with words by\n       <a href="/wiki/Yevgeniy_Dolmatovsky" title="Yevgeniy Dolmatovsky">\n        Yevgeniy Dolmatovsky\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some sources have claimed that Gagarin commented during the flight, "I don\'t see any God up here." However, no such words appear in the verbatim record of his conversations with Earth-based stations during the spaceflight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosmoworld_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cosmoworld-25">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In a 2006 interview, Gagarin\'s friend Colonel Valentin Petrov stated that the cosmonaut never said such words, and that the quote originated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">\n        Nikita Khrushchev\n       </a>\n       \'s speech at the plenum of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_CPSU" title="Central Committee of the CPSU">\n        Central Committee of the CPSU\n       </a>\n       about the state\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/USSR_anti-religious_campaign_(1958%E2%80%931964)" title="USSR anti-religious campaign (1958\xe2\x80\x931964)">\n        anti-religion campaign\n       </a>\n       , saying "Gagarin flew into space, but didn\'t see any god there."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ir73_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ir73-26">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Petrov also said that Gagarin had been baptised into the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">\n        Orthodox Church\n       </a>\n       as a child, and a 2011\n       <i>\n        Foma\n       </i>\n       magazine article quoted the rector of the Orthodox church in\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_City,_Russia" title="Star City, Russia">\n        Star City\n       </a>\n       saying, "Gagarin baptized his elder daughter Yelena shortly before his space flight; and his family used to celebrate Christmas and Easter and keep icons in the house."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ir8361_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ir8361-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Soviet_space_program">\n        After the Soviet space program\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin\'s flight was a triumph for the Soviet space program. The announcement on the Soviet radio was made by\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Levitan" title="Yuri Levitan">\n        Yuri Levitan\n       </a>\n       , the same speaker who announced all major events in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War" title="Great Patriotic War">\n        Great Patriotic War\n       </a>\n       . Gagarin became a national hero of the Soviet Union and Eastern Bloc, and a worldwide celebrity. Newspapers around the globe published his biography and details of his flight. Moscow and other cities in the USSR held mass demonstrations, the scale of which was second only to\n       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Victory_Parade_of_1945" title="Moscow Victory Parade of 1945">\n        World War II Victory Parades\n       </a>\n       . Gagarin was escorted in a long motorcade of high-ranking officials through the streets of Moscow to the Kremlin where, in a lavish ceremony, he was awarded the title of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">\n        Hero of the Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       , by Nikita Khrushchev.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4089" data-file-width="5306" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg/220px-Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg/330px-Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg/440px-Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yuri_Gagarin_welcome_Warsaw_1961.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Gagarin in\n         <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">\n          Warsaw\n         </a>\n         , 1961\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Later on, Gagarin toured widely abroad. He visited Italy, Germany, Canada, Brazil, Japan, Egypt\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mkegypt_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mkegypt-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Finland to promote the Soviet Union\'s accomplishment of putting the first human in space. He visited the United Kingdom three months after the Vostok 1 mission, going to\n       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">\n        London\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">\n        Manchester\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcml_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wcml-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French1998_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-French1998-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The sudden rise to fame took its toll on Gagarin. While acquaintances say Gagarin had been a "sensible drinker", his touring schedule placed him in social situations where he was always expected to drink. Gagarin was also reportedly caught by his wife in a room with another woman, a nurse named Anna who had aided him after a boating incident earlier in the day, at a Black Sea resort in September 1961. He attempted to escape by leaving through a window and jumping off her second floor balcony, hitting his face on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Curb" title="Curb">\n        kerbstone\n       </a>\n       and leaving a permanent scar above his left eyebrow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indep20110403_6-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-indep20110403-6">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20110404_10-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20110404-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1962, he began serving as a Deputy to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_of_the_Union" title="Soviet of the Union">\n        Soviet of the Union\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redstar20110412_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-redstar20110412-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and was elected to the Central Committee of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Komsomol" title="Komsomol">\n        Young Communist League\n       </a>\n       . He later returned to\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_City,_Russia" title="Star City, Russia">\n        Star City\n       </a>\n       , the cosmonaut facility, where he spent several years working on designs for a reusable spacecraft. He became a\n       <a href="/wiki/Podpolkovnik" title="Podpolkovnik">\n        lieutenant colonel\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Air_Forces" title="Soviet Air Forces">\n        Soviet Air Forces\n       </a>\n       on 12 June 1962, and received the rank of\n       <a href="/wiki/Polkovnik" title="Polkovnik">\n        colonel\n       </a>\n       on 6 November 1963.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astro_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astro-11">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Soviet officials tried to keep him away from any flights, being worried of losing their hero in an accident. Gagarin was backup pilot for his friend\n       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Komarov" title="Vladimir Komarov">\n        Vladimir Komarov\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_1" title="Soyuz 1">\n        Soyuz 1\n       </a>\n       flight, which was launched despite Gagarin\'s protests that additional safety precautions were necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-krulwich2011_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-krulwich2011-33">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When Komarov\'s flight ended in a fatal crash, Gagarin was permanently banned from training for and participating in further spaceflights.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 20 December 1963, Gagarin had become Deputy Training Director of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_City,_Russia" title="Star City, Russia">\n        Star City\n       </a>\n       cosmonaut training base.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronaut.ru_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astronaut.ru-34">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Two years later he was re-elected as a deputy to the SSSU, but this time to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_of_Nationalities" title="Soviet of Nationalities">\n        Soviet of Nationalities\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redstar20110412_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-redstar20110412-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Next year he began to re-qualify as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Fighter_pilot" title="Fighter pilot">\n        fighter pilot\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 17 February 1968, he successfully defended his aerospace engineering thesis on the subject of\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceplane" title="Spaceplane">\n        spaceplane\n       </a>\n       aerodynamic configuration, passing with flying colors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebedev201108_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lebedev201108-36">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebedev201110_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lebedev201110-37">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Death">\n        Death\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG">\n         <img alt="Plaque on a brick wall with inscription: \xd0\xae\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb9 \xd0\x90\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb5\xd0\xba\xd1\x81\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb8\xd1\x87 \xd0\x93\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb3\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd, 1934-03-09\xe2\x80\x931968-03-27" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG/220px-Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG/330px-Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG/440px-Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis_08.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Plaque indicating Gagarin\'s interment in the Kremlin Wall\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 27 March 1968, while on a routine training flight from\n       <a href="/wiki/Chkalovsky_Airport" title="Chkalovsky Airport">\n        Chkalovsky Air Base\n       </a>\n       , he and flight instructor\n       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Seryogin" title="Vladimir Seryogin">\n        Vladimir Seryogin\n       </a>\n       died in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-15" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-15">\n        MiG-15UTI\n       </a>\n       crash near the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kirzhach" title="Kirzhach">\n        Kirzhach\n       </a>\n       . The bodies of Gagarin and Seryogin were cremated and the ashes were buried in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis" title="Kremlin Wall Necropolis">\n        walls of the Kremlin\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">\n        Red Square\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin is survived by his wife Valentina, and daughters Yelena and Galina.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cause_of_jet_crash">\n        Cause of jet crash\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The cause of the crash that killed Gagarin is not entirely certain, and has been subject to speculation about conspiracy theories over the ensuing decades.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Soviet documents declassified in March 2003 showed that the\n       <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">\n        KGB\n       </a>\n       had conducted their own investigation of the accident, in addition to one government and two military investigations. The KGB\'s report dismissed various conspiracy theories, instead indicating that the actions of airbase personnel contributed to the crash. The report states that an\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_controller" title="Air traffic controller">\n        air traffic controller\n       </a>\n       provided Gagarin with outdated weather information, and that by the time of his flight, conditions had deteriorated significantly. Ground crew also left external fuel tanks attached to the aircraft. Gagarin\'s planned flight activities needed clear weather and no outboard tanks. The investigation concluded that Gagarin\'s aircraft entered a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spin_(flight)" title="Spin (flight)">\n        spin\n       </a>\n       , either due to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bird_strike" title="Bird strike">\n        bird strike\n       </a>\n       or because of a sudden move to avoid another aircraft. Because of the out-of-date weather report, the crew believed their altitude to be higher than it actually was, and could not react properly to bring the MiG-15 out of its spin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph080801_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-telegraph080801-38">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another hypothesis, advanced by the original crash investigator in 2005, hypothesizes that a cabin air vent was accidentally left open by the crew or the previous pilot, leading to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxygen_deprivation" title="Oxygen deprivation">\n        oxygen deprivation\n       </a>\n       and leaving the crew incapable of controlling the aircraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ScotlandSunday-GagarinInquiry_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ScotlandSunday-GagarinInquiry-39">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A similar hypothesis, published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Air_%26_Space/Smithsonian" title="Air &amp; Space/Smithsonian">\n         Air &amp; Space\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       magazine, is that the crew detected the open vent and followed procedure by executing a rapid dive to a lower altitude. This dive caused them to lose consciousness and crash.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airspace20100901_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-airspace20100901-40">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 12 April 2007, the Kremlin vetoed a new investigation into the death of Gagarin. Government officials said that they saw no reason to begin a new investigation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-belfast171_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-belfast171-41">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_(10316391126).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="1200" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg/220px-Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg/330px-Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg/440px-Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_%2810316391126%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landing._Mig-15_RA-0488G_(10316391126).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Russian MiG-15UTI, the same type as Gagarin was flying\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In April 2011, documents from a 1968 commission set up by the Central Committee of the Communist Party to investigate the accident were declassified. Those documents revealed that the commission\'s original conclusion was that Gagarin or Seryogin had maneuvered sharply either to avoid a weather balloon, leading the jet into a "super-critical flight regime and to its stalling in complex meteorological conditions," or to avoid "entry into the upper limit of the first layer of cloud cover".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp20110408_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-afp20110408-42">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In his 2004 book\n       <i>\n        Two Sides of the Moon\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov" title="Alexey Leonov">\n        Alexey Leonov\n       </a>\n       , who was part of a State Commission established to investigate the death in 1968, recounts that he was flying a helicopter in the same area that day when he heard "two loud booms in the distance." Corroborating other hypotheses, his conclusion is that a Sukhoi jet (which he identifies as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-15" title="Sukhoi Su-15">\n        Su-15 \'Flagon\'\n       </a>\n       ) was flying below its minimum allowed altitude, and "without realizing it because of the terrible weather conditions, he passed within 10 or 20 meters of Yuri and Seregin\'s plane while breaking the sound barrier." The resulting turbulence would have sent the MiG into an uncontrolled spin. Leonov believes the first boom he heard was that of the jet breaking the sound barrier, and the second was Gagarin\'s plane crashing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeonovBook_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LeonovBook-43">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In a June 2013 interview with Russian television network\n       <a href="/wiki/RT_(TV_network)" title="RT (TV network)">\n        RT\n       </a>\n       , Leonov said that a declassified report on the incident revealed the presence of a second, "unauthorized" Su-15 flying in the area. Leonov states that this aircraft had descended to 450 metres (1,480\xc2\xa0ft) and that, while running afterburners, "the aircraft reduced its echelon at a distance of 10\xe2\x80\x9315 meters in the clouds, passing close to Gagarin, turning his plane and thus sending it into a tailspin \xe2\x80\x93 a deep spiral, to be precise \xe2\x80\x93 at a speed of 750 kilometers per hour." As a condition of being allowed to discuss the report, however, Leonov was required to not disclose the name of the other pilot, who was reported to be 80 years old (as of 2013) and in poor health.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rt20130614_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rt20130614-44">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unitoday20130614_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-unitoday20130614-45">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">\n        Personal life\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In 1957, while at the First Chkalov Air Force Pilot\'s School in\n       <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">\n        Orenburg\n       </a>\n       , Gagarin met Valentina Ivanovna Goryacheva,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenberg-About_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rosenberg-About-5">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a medical technician graduate of the Orenburg Medical School.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20110404_10-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20110404-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They were married on 7 November 1957, the same day Gagarin graduated from Orenburg.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       They had two daughters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenberg-About_5-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rosenberg-About-5">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eandt20110314_8-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eandt20110314-8">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Yelena Yurievna Gagarina is an art historian who has worked as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Director-general" title="Director-general">\n        Director-General\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">\n        Moscow Kremlin\n       </a>\n       Museums since 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airspace20110501_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-airspace20110501-46">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euronews20110412_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-euronews20110412-47">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galina Yurievna Gagarina is a professor of economics and the department chair at\n       <a href="/wiki/Plekhanov_Russian_University_of_Economics" title="Plekhanov Russian University of Economics">\n        Plekhanov Russian University of Economics\n       </a>\n       in Moscow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airspace20110501_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-airspace20110501-46">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rea20110411_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rea20110411-48">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_tributes">\n        Legacy and tributes\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">\n        Legacy\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Aside from his short stature at 1.57 metres (5\xc2\xa0ft 2\xc2\xa0in), one of Gagarin\'s most notable traits was his smile.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20110307_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20110307-49">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many commented on how Gagarin\'s smile gained the attention of crowds on the frequent tours he did in the months after the Vostok 1 mission success.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French1998_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-French1998-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin also garnered a reputation as an adept public figure. When he visited\n       <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">\n        Manchester\n       </a>\n       in the United Kingdom, it was pouring rain. However, Gagarin insisted that the convertible top remain down so that the cheering crowds could catch a glimpse of him. Gagarin stated, "If all these people have turned out to welcome me and can stand in the rain, so can I." Gagarin refused an\n       <a href="/wiki/Umbrella" title="Umbrella">\n        umbrella\n       </a>\n       and remained standing in his open-top\n       <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">\n        Bentley\n       </a>\n       so that the cheering crowds could still see him.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French1998_31-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-French1998-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Korolev" title="Sergei Korolev">\n        Sergei Korolev\n       </a>\n       , one of the masterminds behind the early years of the Soviet space program, later said that Gagarin possessed a smile "that lit up the Cold War".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20110313_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-guardian20110313-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes">\n        Tributes\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1563" data-file-width="1563" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG/220px-10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG/330px-10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG/440px-10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10_Rouble_2001-2.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Russian Rouble commemorating Gagarin in 2001\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gagarin_statue_london.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="532" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Gagarin_statue_london.jpg/220px-Gagarin_statue_london.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Gagarin_statue_london.jpg/330px-Gagarin_statue_london.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Gagarin_statue_london.jpg/440px-Gagarin_statue_london.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gagarin_statue_london.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Yuri Gagarin\n         </i>\n         statue in London, near Admiralty Arch (now in Greenwich)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg/220px-Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg/330px-Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg/440px-Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yuri_Gagarin-Wayside_Dr_Statue1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          John Glenn\n         </i>\n         panel and\n         <i>\n          Yuri Gagarin\n         </i>\n         statue in Houston, at the former NASA office on Wayside Drive\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       12 April, the date of Gagarin\'s space flight, has been commemorated as a special date. Since 1962, it has been celebrated in the USSR and later in Russia and other post-Soviet states as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day" title="Cosmonautics Day">\n        Cosmonautics Day\n       </a>\n       . In 2011 it was declared the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Day_of_Human_Space_Flight" title="International Day of Human Space Flight">\n        International Day of Human Space Flight\n       </a>\n       by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since 2001,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri%27s_Night" title="Yuri\'s Night">\n        Yuri\'s Night\n       </a>\n       , an international celebration, is held every 12 April to commemorate milestones in space exploration.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of buildings and other sites on Earth have been named for Gagarin. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin_Cosmonaut_Training_Center" title="Yuri Gagarin Cosmonaut Training Center">\n        Cosmonaut Training Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_City,_Russia" title="Star City, Russia">\n        Star City\n       </a>\n       was named in 1969. The launch pad at\n       <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">\n        Baikonur Cosmodrome\n       </a>\n       from which\n       <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">\n        Sputnik 1\n       </a>\n       and Vostok 1 were launched, is now known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin%27s_Start" title="Gagarin\'s Start">\n        Gagarin\'s Start\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gagarin_Raion" title="Gagarin Raion">\n        Gagarin Raion\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">\n        Sevastopol\n       </a>\n       city (\n       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">\n        Ukraine\n       </a>\n       ) was named after him during the period of the Soviet Union. The Air Force Academy was renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Air_Force_Academy" title="Gagarin Air Force Academy">\n        Gagarin Air Force Academy\n       </a>\n       in 1968.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin has been honored on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Moon\n       </a>\n       by both astronauts and astronomers. He was honored by the American space program during\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n        Apollo 11\n       </a>\n       in 1969 when astronauts\n       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">\n        Neil Armstrong\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">\n        Buzz Aldrin\n       </a>\n       left a memorial satchel containing medals commemorating Gagarin and fellow cosmonaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Komarov" title="Vladimir Komarov">\n        Vladimir Komarov\n       </a>\n       on the surface.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo20090721_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-natgeo20090721-52">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aldrin1989_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aldrin1989-53">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1971,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">\n        Apollo 15\n       </a>\n       astronauts\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">\n        David Scott\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Irwin" title="James Irwin">\n        James Irwin\n       </a>\n       left the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fallen_Astronaut" title="Fallen Astronaut">\n         Fallen Astronaut\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       at their landing site as a memorial to all the American astronauts and Soviet cosmonauts who died in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">\n        Space Race\n       </a>\n       , with Yuri Gagarin listed among 14 others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geppert2012_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Geppert2012-54">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slate20131216_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-slate20131216-55">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He is memorialized by the official naming of a 265\xc2\xa0km\n       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_(crater)" title="Gagarin (crater)">\n        crater on the Far Side\n       </a>\n       after him.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several statues have been erected in his honor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 4 June 1980, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_Yuri_Gagarin" title="Monument to Yuri Gagarin">\n        monument to Gagarin\n       </a>\n       was opened on Gagarin Square in\n       <a href="/wiki/Leninsky_Avenue,_Moscow" title="Leninsky Avenue, Moscow">\n        Leninsky Avenue, Moscow\n       </a>\n       . The monument is 42.4 m tall and constructed of titanium. Beside the column is a replica of the descent module used by Gagarin.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2011 a statue,\n       <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Yuri_Gagarin,_Greenwich" title="Statue of Yuri Gagarin, Greenwich">\n        <i>\n         Yuri Gagarin\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , was unveiled at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Arch" title="Admiralty Arch">\n        Admiralty Arch\n       </a>\n       end of\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Mall,_London" title="The Mall, London">\n        The Mall\n       </a>\n       in London, opposite the permanent sculpture of\n       <a href="/wiki/File:James_Cook_statue_569r.jpg" title="File:James Cook statue 569r.jpg">\n        James Cook\n       </a>\n       . It is a copy of the statue outside Gagarin\'s former school in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lyubertsy" title="Lyubertsy">\n        Lyubertsy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20110406_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-guardian20110406-56">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2013 the statue was moved to a permanent location outside the\n       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich" title="Royal Observatory, Greenwich">\n        Royal Observatory\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">\n        Greenwich\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ria20130307_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ria20130307-57">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2012, a statue was unveiled at the site of NASA\'s original spaceflight headquarters on South Wayside Drive in\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       . The sculpture, completed in 2011 by artist/cosmonaut\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexsei_Leonov" title="Alexsei Leonov">\n        Alexsei Leonov\n       </a>\n       , was a gift to Houston by various Russian organisations. Houston Mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Annise_Parker" title="Annise Parker">\n        Annise Parker\n       </a>\n       , NASA Administrator\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bolden" title="Charles Bolden">\n        Charles Bolden\n       </a>\n       , and Russian Ambassador\n       <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Kislyak" title="Sergey Kislyak">\n        Sergey Kislyak\n       </a>\n       were present for the dedication.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonstatue_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-houstonstatue-58">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gagarin is memorialized in music, including a\n       <a href="/wiki/Song_cycle" title="Song cycle">\n        cycle\n       </a>\n       of Soviet patriotic songs\n       <i>\n        The Constellation Gagarin\n       </i>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="ru">\n        \xd0\xa1\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb7\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb7\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb5 \xd0\x93\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb3\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <small>\n        <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">\n         tr.\n        </a>\n       </small>\n       <i>\n        Sozvezdie Gagarina\n       </i>\n       ) was written by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexandra_Pakhmutova" title="Alexandra Pakhmutova">\n        Alexandra Pakhmutova\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Dobronravov" title="Nikolai Dobronravov">\n        Nikolai Dobronravov\n       </a>\n       in 1970\xe2\x80\x931971.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakhmutova_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pakhmutova-59">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The most famous of these songs referred to Gagarin\'s\n       <i>\n        poekhali!\n       </i>\n       :\n       <i>\n        He said "let\'s go!" He waved his hand\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dushenko_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dushenko-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakhmutova_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pakhmutova-59">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He was the inspiration for the pieces "Hey Gagarin" by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Michel_Jarre" title="Jean Michel Jarre">\n        Jean Michel Jarre\n       </a>\n       (on\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tamorphoses" title="M\xc3\xa9tamorphoses">\n         M\xc3\xa9tamorphoses\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), "Gagarin" by\n       <a href="/wiki/Public_Service_Broadcasting_(band)" title="Public Service Broadcasting (band)">\n        Public Service Broadcasting\n       </a>\n       , and "Gagarin, I loved you" by\n       <a href="/wiki/Undervud" title="Undervud">\n        Undervud\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Vessels have been named for him. Soviet\n       <a href="/wiki/Tracking_ship" title="Tracking ship">\n        tracking ship\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Kosmonavt_Yuri_Gagarin" title="Kosmonavt Yuri Gagarin">\n         Kosmonavt Yuri Gagarin\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was built in 1971.\n       <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">\n        Armenian\n       </a>\n       airline\n       <a href="/wiki/Armavia" title="Armavia">\n        Armavia\n       </a>\n       named their first\n       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Superjet_100" title="Sukhoi Superjet 100">\n        Sukhoi Superjet 100\n       </a>\n       in Gagarin\'s honour in 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flight20110115_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-flight20110115-60">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commemorative_coins_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Commemorative coins of the Soviet Union">\n        two commemorative coins\n       </a>\n       issued in the Soviet Union to honour the 20th and 30th anniversaries of his flight: 1\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_ruble" title="Soviet ruble">\n        ruble\n       </a>\n       coin (1981, copper-nickel) and 3 ruble coin (1991, silver). In 2001, to commemorate the 40th anniversary of Gagarin\'s flight, a series of four coins bearing his likeness was issued in Russia: 2\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">\n        ruble\n       </a>\n       coin (copper-nickel), 3 ruble coin (silver), 10 ruble coin (brass-copper, nickel), and 100 ruble coin (silver).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbr_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cbr-61">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2011, Russia issued a 1,000 ruble coin (gold) and 3 ruble coin (silver) to mark the 50th anniversary of his flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coinupdate_62-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-coinupdate-62">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2008, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">\n        Kontinental Hockey League\n       </a>\n       named their championship trophy the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Cup" title="Gagarin Cup">\n        Gagarin Cup\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spm100519_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spm100519-63">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In a 2010\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Foundation" title="Space Foundation">\n        Space Foundation\n       </a>\n       survey, Gagarin was ranked as the #6 most popular space hero, tied with\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">\n         Star Trek\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\n        \'\n       </span>\n       s fictional Capt.\n       <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">\n        James T. Kirk\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacefoundation_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spacefoundation-64">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Russian docudrama,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gagarin:_First_in_Space" title="Gagarin: First in Space">\n         Gagarin: First in Space\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , was released in 2013.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="50th_anniversary">\n        50th anniversary\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_2011_Gagarin_(1).JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="224" data-file-width="455" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG/220px-Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG/330px-Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG/440px-Stamp_2011_Gagarin_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_2011_Gagarin_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         50th anniversary stamp of\n         <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">\n          Ukraine\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The 50th anniversary of Gagarin\'s journey into space was marked in 2011 by tributes around the world. A film titled\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/First_Orbit" title="First Orbit">\n         First Orbit\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was shot from the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       , combining the original flight audio with footage of the route taken by Gagarin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20110411_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-guardian20110411-65">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Russian, American, and Italian\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_27" title="Expedition 27">\n        Expedition 27\n       </a>\n       crew aboard the ISS sent a special video message to wish the people of the world a "Happy\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri%27s_Night" title="Yuri\'s Night">\n        Yuri\'s Night\n       </a>\n       ", wearing shirts with an image of Gagarin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube20110411_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-youtube20110411-66">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Swiss-based German watchmaker Bernhard Lederer created a limited edition of 50 Gagarin Tourbillons to commemorate the 50th anniversary of Yuri Gagarin\'s flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourbillon_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tourbillon-67">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-21" title="Soyuz TMA-21">\n        Soyuz TMA-21\n       </a>\n       on 4 April 2011 was devoted to the 50th anniversary of the first manned space mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mannedaero_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mannedaero-68">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_awards">\n        Honours and awards\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" </a>\n         , Serbia.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Medal_%2240_Years_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_the_USSR%22" title=\'Jubilee
